كتاب الديات
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ سکتا ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک عاقلہ ہونے کا مدار قرابت پر نہیں بلکہ نصرت پر ہے اسی نصرت کی وجہ سے اہل دیوان پر دیت واجب ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی لشکر کے جون سے محکمہ میں اس کا نام درج ہے وہ اس کے اہل دیوان میں جو اس کی مدد کے ذمہ دار ہیں لہذا انہیں پر دیت واجب ہوگی ۔ اہلِ دیوان کی تفصیل کتاب المعاقل میں آرہی ہے۔
امام شافعی کے استدلال کا جواب
بخلاف الذمى لأنهم لايتعاقلون فيما بينهم فلا عاقلة فتجب في ذمته صيانة للدم عن الهدر وبخلاف الجناية على المال لأن العواقل لاتعقل المال إلا أنه يخير بين الدفع والفداء لأنه واحد وفي إثبات الخيرة نوع تخفيف في حقه كيلا يستأصل
ترجمہ بخلاف ذمی کے اس لئے کہ وہ آپس میں دیت نہیں دیتے تو ان کی کوئی مددگار برادری نہیں ہے تو دیت ذمی کے ذمہ میں واجب ہوگی خون کو ہدر سے بچاتے ہوئے اور بخلاف مال پر جنایت کرنے کے اس لئے کہ برادری والے مال کی دیت نہیں دیا کرتے مگر آقاء کو اختیار دیا جائے گا غلام کو دینے اور فدیہ دینے کے درمیان اس لئے کہ آقا ایک ہے اور اختیار کو ثابت کرنے میں اس کے حق میں تخفیف ہے تا کہ وہ ہلاک نہ کر دیا جائے۔ تشریح امام شافعی نے جو ذمی سے استدلال کیا ہے وہ درست نہیں ہے کیونکہ ذمیوں میں آپس میں دیت دینے کا اور ایک دوسرے کی مدد کرنے کا رواج ہی نہیں ہے تو جب ذمی کا کوئی عاقلہ ہی نہیں ہے تو اس کے علاوہ کوئی چارہ کار نہیں ہے کہ جرم کی سزا کو خود ذمی پر واجب کر دیا جائے تا کہ مجنی علیہ کے خون کو رائیگاں کرنالازم نہ آئے ۔
نیز امام شافعی نے جو مال پر جنایت سے استدلال کیا ہے وہ بھی درست نہیں کیونکہ مددگار برادری مال کی دیت نہیں دیا کرتی بلکہ فقط نفس کی دیت دیا کرتی ہے تو اس سے استشہاد کیسا ! پھر مولی اکیلا ہے جماعت نہیں ہے تا کہ اس کو زیادہ پریشانی لاحق نہ ہو بغرض تخفیف اس کو یہ اختیار دیدیا گیا کہ چاہے غلام کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دے اور چاہے تو غلام کافر یہ ادا کر دے۔
حنفیہ کے مسلک کی وضاحت
غير أن الواجب الأصلى هو الدافع فى الصحيح ولهذا يسقط الموجب بموت العبد لفوات محل الواجب وإن كان له حق النقل إلى الفداء كما فى مال الزكاة بخلاف موت الجانى الحر لأن الواجب لا يتعلق بالحر استيفاء فصار كالعبد في صدقة الفطر
ترجمہ ۔ علاوہ اس بات کے کہ واجب اصلی وہ غلام دینا ہے صحیح روایت کے مطابق اور اسی وجہ سے موجب ساقط ہو جاتا ہے غلام کی موت سے محل واجب کے فوت ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر چہ آقا کو فدیہ ادا کرنے کی جانب انتقال کا حق ہے جیسے زکوۃ کے مال میں بخلاف آزاد جانی کی موت کے ، اس لئے کہ واجب آزاد کے ساتھ متعلق نہیں ہوتا وصولیابی کے اعتبار سے تو ایسا ہو گیا جیسے صدقہ فطر میں غلام ۔ تشریح اختلاف سے فارغ ہو کر مصنف یہ بیان فرماتے ہیں کہ حنفیہ کے نزدیک آقاء کو اختیار ہے کہ چاہے غلام ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دے اور چاہے اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ اصل واجب کیا ہے۔
تو فرمایا کہ اگر چہ تمرتاش کی روایت میں دیت کو اصلی واجب کا ہے مگر صحیح یہ ہے کہ اصل واجب غلام دینا ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر ابھی آقا نے کچھ اختیار نہیں کیا تھا کہ وہ غلام ہی مر گیا تو اب آقا پر کچھ واجب نہیں رہا کیونکہ محل واجب ہی فوت ہو گیا ہے، اگر دیت اصل واجب ہوتی تو وہ ختم نہ ہونی چاہیئے تھی۔
تو جیسے مال زکوۃ میں اصل تو یہ ہے کہ نصاب ہی کا جز مقر ر ادا کرے لیکن شرعاً اس کو یہ اجازت دے دی گئی کہ اگر چاہے دوسرے مال سے اتنی مقدار کو ادا کر دے، اور اگر مال نصاب ہلاک ہو جائے تو محل واجب کے فوات کی وجہ سے زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
اسی طرح یہاں کا مسئلہ ہے کہ اصل واجب دفع غلام ہے لیکن اگر آقا اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے تو جائز ہے۔ لیکن یہ مسئلہ کہ مجرم کے مرنے سے جرمانہ ساقط ہو جائے گا فقط غلام مجرم کے لئے ہے، اور اگر مجرم آزار مر اور وہ مر جائے تو واجب ختم نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ مقدار اجب کی ادائیگی کا تعلق ذات مجرم سے نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے مال سے ہے اور مال مرنے کا بعد بھی موجود ہے اور اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے جیسے شوال کی پہلی تاریخ میں سے صبح صادق کے طلوع کے بعد آقا کا غلام مر گیا تو غلام کی موت کی وجہ سے اس کا صدقہ فطر آقا کے اوپر سے ساقط نہ ہوگا، بلکہ واجب الادا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ غلام کے مرنے سے محل واجب ختم نہیں ہوا بلکہ محل واجب تو آقا کا مال ہے جو اس کی موت کے بعد بھی موجود ہے۔
آقا کو کیا چیز دینے کا اختیار ہے
قال فإن دفعه ملكه ولى الجناية وإن فداه فداه بارشها وكل ذالك يلزمه حالا أما الدفع فلأن التاجيل في الأعيان باطل وعند اختياره الواجب عين وأما الفداء فلأنه جعل بدلا عن العبد فى الشرع وإن كان مقدرا بالمتلف ولهذا سمى فداء فيقوم مقامه ويأخذ حكمه فلهذا وجب حالا كالمبدل ترجمه نام قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر آقا نے عبد جانی کو دیدیا تو ولی جنایت اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا ۔ اور اگر آقا ء اس کا فدیہ دینا منظور کرے تو جنایت کے ارش کے مطابق اس کا فدیہ ادا کرے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک آقا کو فی الحال لازم ہوگا ، بہر حال غلام دینا پس اس لئے کہ اعیان میں تاجیل باطل ہے اور مولی کے اختیار کرنے کے وقت غلام دینے کو جو چیز واجب ہے وہ عین ہے اور بہر حال فدیہ دینا پس اس لئے کہ وہ شریعت میں غلام کا بدل قرار دیا گیا ہے اگر چہ وہ مختلف کے ساتھ مقدر ہے اسی وجہ سے اس کا نام فدیہ رکھا جاتا ہے پس فدیہ غلام کے قائم مقام ہو گا اور غلام کے حکم کو لے لیگا ہیں اسی وجہ سے مبدل کے مثل بدل ( فدیہ ) فی الحال واجب ہوگا ۔
تشریح مصنف نے یہاں تین باتیں بیان فرمائی ہیں
- جب آقا نے غلام کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا تو ولی جنابیت غلام کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ - جب آقا فدیہ دینا منظور کرے تو فدیہ اتنادے گا جو جنایت کے ارش کے بقدر ہوگا۔ - غلام دے خواہ فدیہ دے اس کی ادائیگی فی الحال واجب ہوگی ۔
Kitab al-Diyat. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 15. It can be, and according to us the basis of being 'aqila is not kinship but support. Due to this support, blood money is obligatory on the people of the register (ahl al-diwan), i.e., those whose name is recorded in the military department, who are responsible for his assistance. Hence, blood money will be obligatory on them. Details of ahl al-diwan will come in the Book of al-Mawaqil. The rebuttal of Imam Shafi'i's argument: "Unlike the dhimmi, because they do not pay blood money among themselves, so they have no 'aqila. Thus it is obligatory on his dhimmah to preserve the blood from being wasted. And unlike the crime against property, because the 'aqila do not pay blood money for property. However, he (the master) is given a choice between handing over and ransom because he is one (individual), and in establishing the choice there is a type of leniency in his favor so that he is not annihilated." Translation: Unlike the dhimmi, because they do not pay blood money among themselves, so they have no supporting kinship. Thus, blood money becomes obligatory on the dhimmi's liability to prevent the blood of the victim from being wasted. And unlike the crime against property, because the supporting kinship does not pay blood money for property. But the master will be given a choice between handing over the slave and paying ransom because the master is one (individual), and establishing this choice is a leniency in his favor so that he is not ruined. Explanation: The argument that Imam Shafi'i made using the dhimmi is not correct because dhimmis do not practice paying blood money among themselves nor assisting each other. So when a dhimmi has no 'aqila, there is no alternative but to make the punishment for the crime obligatory on the dhimmi himself so that the blood of the victim is not wasted. Also, the argument Imam Shafi'i made using the crime against property is also not correct because the supporting kinship does not pay blood money for property; they only pay blood money for the soul (life). So how can it be used as evidence? Furthermore, the master is alone, not a group, so to avoid excessive hardship for him, as a leniency, he is given this choice: either hand over the slave to the victim's guardian or pay a ransom for the slave. Clarification of the Hanafi school's position: "Except that the primary obligation is the handing over (of the slave) in the correct view; and for this reason the obligation drops with the death of the slave due to the loss of the subject of the obligation, even though he (the master) has the right to transfer to ransom, as in zakat property. Contrary to the death of the free criminal, because the obligation is not attached to the free person in terms of execution; thus it is like the slave in sadaqat al-fitr." Translation: Besides that, the primary obligation is the handing over of the slave according to the correct narration, and for this reason the obligation drops with the death of the slave due to the loss of the subject of the obligation, although the master has the right to transfer to paying ransom, like in zakat property. Unlike the death of the free criminal, because the obligation is not attached to the free person in terms of execution; so it becomes like the slave in sadaqat al-fitr. Explanation: Having finished with the disagreement, the author states that according to the Hanafis, the master has a choice: either hand over the slave to the victim's guardian or pay his ransom. But the question is: what is the primary obligation? So he said that although in the narration of Tamurtash, blood money is considered the primary obligation, but the correct view is that the primary obligation is to hand over the slave. The proof is that if the master had not yet made a choice and the slave dies, then nothing remains obligatory on the master because the subject of the obligation has been lost. If blood money were the primary obligation, it should not have dropped. So it is similar to zakat property: the primary thing is that one should give a specific part of the nisab itself, but the Law has permitted him that if he wishes, he may give that amount from other property. And if the nisab property is destroyed, the zakat drops due to the loss of the subject of the obligation. Similarly here, the primary obligation is to hand over the slave, but if the master pays his ransom, it is permissible. However, this rule (that the penalty drops with the death of the criminal) is only for the slave criminal. If the free criminal dies, the obligation does not drop because the payment of the obligatory amount is not attached to the person of the criminal but to his property, and the property still exists after death. Its exact example is that if a master's slave dies after the break of dawn on the first day of Shawwal, the sadaqat al-fitr for that slave does not drop from the master; rather it remains obligatory. Because the death of the slave did not cause the subject of the obligation to cease; rather the subject of the obligation is the master's property, which still exists after the slave's death. What the master has the authority to give: "He said: If he hands him over, the victim's guardian becomes his owner. And if he ransoms him, he ransoms him with its arsh (equivalent). And all that is binding on him immediately. As for handing over, because deferment (tajil) in specific things is invalid, and when he chooses, what is obligatory is the specific thing ('ayn). As for the ransom, because it is made a substitute for the slave in the Law, even though it is estimated by the value of the destroyed thing. For this reason it is called ransom, and it takes the place of the slave and takes his ruling. Therefore it is obligatory immediately like the substituted thing (mubdal)." Translation: Imam al-Quduri said: If the master hands over the criminal slave, then the victim's guardian becomes his owner. And if the master chooses to pay the ransom, he pays the ransom equal to the arsh of the crime. And each of these is immediately binding on the master. As for handing over the slave, because deferment in specific things is invalid, and at the time of the master's choice, what is obligatory is a specific thing. As for paying the ransom, because it is made a substitute for the slave in the Law, even though it is estimated by the value of the destroyed thing; for this reason it is called ransom. So the ransom stands in the place of the slave and takes his ruling. Hence it is immediately obligatory like the substituted thing. Explanation: The author has stated three things here: 1) When the master hands over the slave to the victim's guardian, the victim's guardian becomes the owner of the slave. 2) If the master chooses to pay the ransom, he pays the ransom equal to the arsh of the crime. 3) Whether he gives the slave or pays the ransom, its payment is obligatory immediately.
Source pages p. 258

Commentary
This passage, from Ashraf al-Hidayah's commentary on Kitab al-Diyat, deals with the liability for crimes committed by slaves and the role of the 'aqila (supporting group). The author begins by clarifying the Hanafi position on 'aqila: its basis is not kinship but support (nusrah), which is why the 'aqila are the people of the military register (ahl al-diwan). This sets the stage for the dispute with Imam Shafi'i. Shafi'i had argued by analogy: just as a dhimmi's blood money is on his own liability (since he has no 'aqila), and just as for crimes against property the slave is given as substitute, so too for homicide by a slave, the master should have no 'aqila but should be solely liable. The Hanafi response counters both analogies. First, dhimmis do not have a practice of mutual blood money payment, so the case is exceptional; for Muslims, the 'aqila system exists and applies. Second, the 'aqila do not pay for property crimes, only for homicide, so the analogy fails. Moreover, the master is alone, not a group, so leniency (the choice between handing over the slave or paying ransom) is granted to avoid his ruin. The commentary then clarifies the intra-Hanafi issue of the primary obligation. Although some narrations (like that of Tamurtash) treat the blood money (diyah) as primary, the correct Hanafi position (as per al-Hidayah) is that handing over the slave (al-daf') is the original obligation. Evidence: if the slave dies before the master's choice, the obligation drops entirely — this would not happen if the primary obligation were a financial payment. This is analogized to zakat on nisab property: the original obligation is to give from the specific nisab, but the owner may substitute other property; if the nisab is destroyed, zakat drops. Similarly, for a free criminal, the obligation does not drop upon death because it attaches to his estate, not his person. The passage concludes with the ruling from Imam al-Quduri: the master may either hand over the slave (immediate transfer of ownership) or pay ransom (equal to the arsh, or estimated value). Both options are immediately binding (hālan) because deferment is invalid in specific property, and the ransom, though monetary, is a substitute standing in the slave's place.

Key Terms
عاقلہ (‘āqila): The group of supporters (usually male relatives or fellow soldiers) who pay blood money on behalf of a killer.
ذمی (dhimmī): A non-Muslim subject living under Muslim rule in a covenant of protection.
فدیہ (fidya): Ransom paid by the master in lieu of handing over the slave who committed a crime.
ارش (arsh): The monetary compensation for a crime against a limb or for the value of a slave when ransom is chosen.
دفع (daf‘): Handing over the criminal slave to the victim's guardian.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if the master has not yet made a choice and the criminal slave dies?
A) The master must pay the blood money from his own property.
B) The obligation drops entirely because the subject (the slave) is gone.
C) The master's 'āqila becomes liable for the blood money.
D) The master's obligation transfers to the slave's estate.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school gives the master the option to hand over the slave or pay ransom, with handing over as the primary obligation; the 'āqila is based on support, not kinship.

Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
The Master's Option in Slave's Crime: Original Obligation and Timing
Establishes master's obligation to hand over slave or pay ransom immediately

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct Hanafi position on the original obligation (asl wajib) when a master's slave commits a crime and explain why payment is immediate.

Core Idea
The master must either hand over the slave or pay ransom immediately—the slave himself is the original obligation.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a key point in Hanafi diyat law: when a slave commits a crime, the master has an option, but the underlying obligation is to hand over the slave. The timing of payment is immediate, not deferred. The commentary uses qiyas with zakat to prove that the slave is the subject of obligation, and an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding whether diyah is original is resolved in favor of handing over the slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's options
State the two choices the master has when his slave commits a crime: hand over the slave or pay ransom (fidyah) equal to the arsh.
Both options are recognized by the text.
2
Determine the original obligation (asl wajib)
According to the correct (sahih) view, the original obligation is to hand over the slave. A contrary riwayah from Tamartash considers diyah as original, but the text refutes this.
The original wajib is the slave himself ('ayn).
3
Understand the proof via qiyas with zakat
Just as in zakat the original obligation is to give from the nisab itself, and if the nisab perishes the obligation lapses, here if the slave dies before the master chooses, the obligation lapses. This proves the slave is the subject.
If diyah were original, the obligation would not lapse with the slave's death.
4
Recognize the timing of payment
Both handing over the slave and paying fidyah are due immediately (halan). Deferment is invalid for specific objects ('ayn), and the substitute takes the same ruling.
The master cannot defer payment once he chooses.
5
Apply the rule to death scenarios
If the slave dies before the master chooses, the obligation lapses. If the master chooses fidyah and then the slave dies, the obligation transfers to the master's dhimma and remains.
This distinction follows from the nature of the wajib.

كر دے اور چاہے اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے لیکن سوال یہ ہے کہ اصل واجب کیا ہے۔
تو فرمایا کہ اگر چہ تمرتاش کی روایت میں دیت کو اصلی واجب کا ہے مگر صحیح یہ ہے کہ اصل واجب غلام دینا ہے۔ اور اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اگر ابھی آقا نے کچھ اختیار نہیں کیا تھا کہ وہ غلام ہی مر گیا تو اب آقا پر کچھ واجب نہیں رہا کیونکہ محل واجب ہی فوت ہو گیا ہے، اگر دیت اصل واجب ہوتی تو وہ ختم نہ ہونی چاہیئے تھی۔
تو جیسے مال زکوۃ میں اصل تو یہ ہے کہ نصاب ہی کا جز مقر ر ادا کرے لیکن شرعاً اس کو یہ اجازت دے دی گئی کہ اگر چاہے دوسرے مال سے اتنی مقدار کو ادا کر دے، اور اگر مال نصاب ہلاک ہو جائے تو محل واجب کے فوات کی وجہ سے زکوۃ ساقط ہو جائے گی۔
اسی طرح یہاں کا مسئلہ ہے کہ اصل واجب دفع غلام ہے لیکن اگر آقا اس کا فدیہ ادا کر دے تو جائز ہے۔ لیکن یہ مسئلہ کہ مجرم کے مرنے سے جرمانہ ساقط ہو جائے گا فقط غلام مجرم کے لئے ہے، اور اگر مجرم آزار مر اور وہ مر جائے تو واجب ختم نہ ہوگا، کیونکہ مقدار اجب کی ادائیگی کا تعلق ذات مجرم سے نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے مال سے ہے اور مال مرنے کا بعد بھی موجود ہے اور اس کی مثال بعینہ ایسی ہے جیسے شوال کی پہلی تاریخ میں سے صبح صادق کے طلوع کے بعد آقا کا غلام مر گیا تو غلام کی موت کی وجہ سے اس کا صدقہ فطر آقا کے اوپر سے ساقط نہ ہوگا، بلکہ واجب الادا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ غلام کے مرنے سے محل واجب ختم نہیں ہوا بلکہ محل واجب تو آقا کا مال ہے جو اس کی موت کے بعد بھی موجود ہے۔
آقا کو کیا چیز دینے کا اختیار ہے
قال فإن دفعه ملكه ولى الجناية وإن فداه فداه بارشها وكل ذالك يلزمه حالا أما الدفع فلأن التاجيل في الأعيان باطل وعند اختياره الواجب عين وأما الفداء فلأنه جعل بدلا عن العبد فى الشرع وإن كان مقدرا بالمتلف ولهذا سمى فداء فيقوم مقامه ويأخذ حكمه فلهذا وجب حالا كالمبدل ترجمه نام قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر آقا نے عبد جانی کو دیدیا تو ولی جنایت اس کا مالک ہو جائے گا ۔ اور اگر آقا ء اس کا فدیہ دینا منظور کرے تو جنایت کے ارش کے مطابق اس کا فدیہ ادا کرے اور ان میں سے ہر ایک آقا کو فی الحال لازم ہوگا ، بہر حال غلام دینا پس اس لئے کہ اعیان میں تاجیل باطل ہے اور مولی کے اختیار کرنے کے وقت غلام دینے کو جو چیز واجب ہے وہ عین ہے اور بہر حال فدیہ دینا پس اس لئے کہ وہ شریعت میں غلام کا بدل قرار دیا گیا ہے اگر چہ وہ مختلف کے ساتھ مقدر ہے اسی وجہ سے اس کا نام فدیہ رکھا جاتا ہے پس فدیہ غلام کے قائم مقام ہو گا اور غلام کے حکم کو لے لیگا ہیں اسی وجہ سے مبدل کے مثل بدل ( فدیہ ) فی الحال واجب ہوگا ۔
تشریح مصنف نے یہاں تین باتیں بیان فرمائی ہیں
- جب آقا نے غلام کو ولی جنایت کے حوالہ کر دیا تو ولی جنابیت غلام کا مالک ہو جائے گا۔ - جب آقا فدیہ دینا منظور کرے تو فدیہ اتنادے گا جو جنایت کے ارش کے بقدر ہوگا۔ - غلام دے خواہ فدیہ دے اس کی ادائیگی فی الحال واجب ہوگی ۔
اب مصنف تیسرے مسئلہ پر دلیل پیش فرماتے ہیں کہ فی الحال ادائیگی کیوں واجب ہوگی تو فرمایا کی تا جیل اس لئے ہوتی ہے تاکہ حق واجی کو فراہم کرنے میں سہولت و آسانی ہو اور یہاں تو غلام پہلے سے موجود ہے، لہذا تا جیل تحصیل حاصل ہے، کیونکہ واجب عین ہے اور اگر فدیہ ادا کرنا چاہے تو فدیہ چونکہ غلام کا بدل ہے اور بدل کا وہی حکم ہو گا جو مبدل کا ہے، لہذا اس کی بھی ادا ئیگی فی الحال واجب ہے اگر چہ فدیہ ارش جنایت کے بقدر ہے لیکن حقیقت میں فدیہ غلام کا بدل ہے۔ اسی لئے تو اس کا نام فدیہ رکھا گیا ہے۔
جس چیز کو آقا نے اختیار کر لیا ولی جنایت کو دوسری چیز اختیار کرنے کا حق نہیں
وأيهما اختاره وفعله لاشيء لولى الجناية غيره أما الدفع فلأن حقه متعلق به فإذا خلى بينه وبين الرقبة سقط وأما الفداء فلأنه لا حق له إلا الأرش فإذا أوفاه حقه سلم العبد له فإن لم يختر شيئا حتى مات العبد بطل حق المجنى عليه لفوات محل حقه على ما بيناه وإن مات بعد ما اختار الفداء لم يبر التحول الحق من رقبة العبد إلى ذمة المولى
ترجمہ اور آقا نے ان دونوں میں سے جس کو اختیار کر لیا اور اس کو انجام دیدیا تو ولی جنایت کے لئے کچھ اس کا غیر نہیں ہے بہر حال غلام دینا پس اس لئے کہ ولی کا حق غلام کے ساتھ متعلق ہے پس جب ولی جنایت اور غلام کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دیا تو مطالبہ کا حق ساقط ہو گیا اور بہر حال فدیہ دینا پس اس لئے کہ ولی کا کوئی حق ارش کے علاوہ نہیں ہے پس جب آقا نے ولی کا حق پورا کر دیا تو غلام آقا کے لئے صحیح سالم رہے گا پس اگر آقا نے کچھ اختیار نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ غلام مر گیا تو مجنی علیہ کا حق باطل ہو گیا، اس کے حق کا محل فوت ہونے کی وجہ نے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر غلام مرا ہو بعد اس کے کہ آقا فدیہ دینا اختیار کرے تو آقا بری نہ ہو گا حق کے متحول ہونے کی وجہ سے غلام کی گردن سے آقا کے ذمہ کی جانب۔ تشریح آقا کو مذکورہ دونوں چیزوں میں اختیار ہے اس نے جو نے کو اختیار کر لیا تو ولی جنایت کا کوئی اور حق نہیں رہا۔ یعنی غلام دیدیا تو ارش کا حق نہیں رہا اور دیتی تو غلام لینے کا حق نہیں رہا۔ کیونکہ غلام دینے کی صورت میں جنایت کا حق غلام کی ذات کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور جب آقا نے غلام اس کو دیدیا تو اس کا حق ادا ہو گیا لہذا اب مزید کے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں رہا اور اگر آقا نے فدیہ ادا کیا ہو تو چونکہ ولی جنایت کا حق بقد را رش تھا جو اس کو مل چکا ہے اور جب ولی کا حق اس کو مل گیا تو غلام آقا کے پاس رہے گا۔ اور ابھی ماقبل میں مسئلہ گذرا ہے کہ اگر غلام مر جائے اور ابھی آقا نے دونوں میں سے کسی کا انتخاب نہیں کیا تھا تو چونکہ اصل واجب غلام ہے اور اب غلام مر گیا ہے لہذا و جوب ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ محل وجوب ختم ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر آقا، فدیہ دینا منظور کر چکا تھا اور پھر غلام مر جائے تو اب فدیہ واجب رہے گا۔ کیونکہ اب دولتی جنایت کا حق غلام سے منتقل ہو کر مدیہ کی جانب آچکا ہے جس کی ادائیگی کا ذمہ دار آتا ہے۔
Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 15. ... [The master] may hand over (the slave) or pay his ransom. But the question is: what is the original obligation? He said: Even though in the narration of Tamartash the diyah is considered the original obligation, the correct view is that the original obligation is to hand over the slave. And its proof is that if the master had not chosen anything and the slave died, then nothing remains obligatory upon the master because the subject of the obligation has perished. If diyah were the original obligation, it should not have lapsed. So just as in the case of zakat property, the original is that one should pay a specific part of the nisab, but the law has given permission that if he wishes, he may pay that amount from other property. And if the nisab property is destroyed, due to the loss of the subject of obligation, the zakat lapses. Similarly, this case is that the original obligation is to hand over the slave, but if the master pays his ransom, it is permissible. But this ruling that the penalty lapses with the death of the offender is only for the slave offender. If the offender is a free person and he dies, the obligation does not lapse, because the payment of the amount is not connected to the person of the offender but to his property, and the property exists after death. And its example is exactly like the case where after the appearance of the true dawn on the first day of Shawwal, the master's slave dies, then due to the slave's death, his sadaqat al-fitr does not lapse from the master, but rather remains obligatory. Because the subject of obligation is not removed by the slave's death; rather the subject of obligation is the master's property which still exists after his death. The master has the option of what to give. He (al-Quduri) said: If he hands him over, the guardian of the crime owns him; and if he ransoms him, he ransoms him with the arsh (compensation) of the crime. And all of that is incumbent upon him immediately. As for handing over, because deferment in specific things is invalid, and when he chooses, the obligatory thing is the 'ayn (specific object). As for the ransom, because it is made a substitute for the slave in the law, even though it is measured by the damaged value, therefore it is called fidyah (ransom). So it stands in his place and takes his ruling, therefore it becomes due immediately like that which is substituted. Translation: Imam Quduri said: Then if the master hands over the slave who committed the crime, the guardian of the crime becomes its owner. And if the master intends to pay his ransom, he pays the ransom according to the arsh of the crime. And each of these is obligatory upon the master immediately. As for handing over the slave, because deferment in specific things is invalid, and at the time of the master's choice, what is obligatory is the 'ayn. As for paying the ransom, because it is made a substitute for the slave in the law, even though it is measured by the damaged value, for this reason it is called fidyah. So the fidyah stands in the place of the slave and takes his ruling; therefore the substitute (fidyah) is obligatory immediately like the substituted (the slave). Explanation: The author has stated three things here: When the master hands over the slave to the guardian, the guardian becomes owner of the slave. When the master intends to pay ransom, he pays as much as the arsh of the crime. Whether he gives the slave or the ransom, its payment is immediately obligatory. Now the author gives proof for the third issue: why payment is immediately obligatory. He said: Deferment is meant to provide ease in fulfilling the right, but here the slave is already present, so deferment is redundant because the wajib is an 'ayn. And if he wants to pay the ransom, the ransom is a substitute for the slave, and the substitute has the same ruling as the substituted, so its payment is also immediately obligatory, even though the ransom is measured by the arsh of the crime, but in reality the ransom is a substitute for the slave. That is why it is called fidyah. Whatever the master chooses, the guardian has no right to the other. He (al-Quduri) said: Whichever of the two he chooses and does, the guardian of the crime has no right to the other. As for handing over, because his right is connected to the slave; when he releases (the slave) to him, the right falls. As for the ransom, because he has no right except the arsh; when he fulfills his right, the slave remains with him. If he does not choose anything until the slave dies, the right of the victim becomes void due to the loss of the subject of his right, as we have explained. And if the slave dies after he has chosen the ransom, he is not discharged because the right has transferred from the slave's neck to the master's liability. Translation: And the master, whichever of these two he chooses and executes, the guardian has no other right. Handing over: because his right is connected to the slave; when he leaves between him and the slave (i.e., hands over possession), the right falls. Ransom: because he has no right except the arsh; when he fulfills his right, the slave remains safe for the master. If the master does not choose anything until the slave died, then the victim's right becomes void due to the loss of the subject of his right, according to the detail we have explained. And if the slave dies after the master has chosen the ransom, the master is not absolved, because the right has transferred from the slave's neck to the master's liability. Explanation: The master has an option between the two things mentioned. Whatever he chooses, the guardian has no other right. That is, if he gives the slave, no right to arsh remains; if he pays the diyah, no right to take the slave remains. Because in the case of handing over the slave, the right of the crime is connected to the slave's person; when the master gives him, his right is fulfilled, so no further right to claim remains. And if the master has paid the ransom, since the guardian's right was the amount of arsh which he has received, when the guardian's right is given to him, the slave remains with the master. And earlier the issue passed that if the slave dies and the master has not yet chosen either, then because the original wajib is the slave and the slave has died, the obligation falls because the subject of obligation is gone. And if the master had intended to pay the ransom and then the slave dies, then the ransom remains obligatory because the right of the crime has transferred from the slave to the master's liability, for which the master is responsible.
Source pages p. 259

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentary of Hidayah, discussing the master's option when his slave commits a crime against another. The text first establishes the underlying obligation (asl wajib): contrary to a narration from Tamartash considering diyah as original, the correct Hanafi position is that the original obligation is to hand over the slave himself. The proof is analogical (qiyas): if the slave dies before the master chooses, the obligation lapses because the subject (the slave) is gone—similar to zakat where if the nisab is destroyed, zakat lapses. If diyah were original, it would not lapse. The master may substitute the slave with fidyah (ransom) equal to the arsh (compensation for the wound), just as in zakat one may pay from other property. The timing of payment is immediate (halan): for handing over the slave, deferment in specific objects is invalid; for fidyah, it takes the same ruling as the substitute. Once the master chooses and executes one option, the victim's guardian has no right to the other. If the master chooses fidyah and the slave dies after that, the obligation does not fall—it transfers from the slave's person to the master's liability (dhimma). This is distinguished from the case of a free offender, where the obligation attaches to his property and survives his death.

Key Terms
ارش (arsh): The specific amount of compensation for a wound or injury inflicted by the slave, which the master pays as fidyah.
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom paid by the master in lieu of handing over the slave; it equals the arsh of the crime.
دیت (diyah): Blood money; in this passage, it refers to the value paid as compensation for the crime, considered by some as the original obligation.
تاجیل (ta'jeel): Deferment of payment. The text states that deferment is invalid (batil) for specific objects ('ayn) because they are already present.
محل واجب (mahall al-wajib): The subject upon which the obligation rests. In this case, it is the slave himself; when he dies, the subject perishes and the obligation lapses unless it has transferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct (sahih) Hanafi position in this passage, what is the original obligation (asl wajib) upon the master when his slave commits a crime?
A) To pay the diyah (blood money) directly.
B) To hand over the slave (the 'ayn) to the victim's guardian.
C) Either to give the slave or pay ransom, at the discretion of the guardian.
D) To pay the amount of arsh as determined by the judge.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the original obligation is to hand over the slave; payment of ransom is a substitute, and both are due immediately.

Master's Choice: Surrender Slave or Pay Ransom
Ruling on master's choice after slave's crime

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the master's two options when his slave commits a crime and explain the legal consequence of each choice, including scenarios of the slave's death.

Core Idea
The master must choose one option; once executed, the guardian's right is exhausted.

When a slave commits a crime against a third party, the master is given a choice: either surrender the slave to the victim's guardian or pay a ransom (fidya). This lesson explains the rulings surrounding this choice, including what happens if the master makes no choice before the slave dies.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's options
The master can either surrender the slave to the guardian (دفع) or pay the ransom (فدیہ). These are the only two options; the guardian cannot demand both.
2
Effect of surrendering the slave
When the master hands over the slave, the guardian's right is attached to the slave's person. Once surrendered, the right is fulfilled and the guardian has no further claim.
3
Effect of paying ransom
If the master pays the ransom, the guardian receives compensation (arash). Since the right is only for compensation, once paid, the slave remains with the master and the guardian's right is satisfied.
4
Slave dies before any choice
If the slave dies before the master chooses anything, the guardian's right becomes void because its subject (the slave) is lost. The right was attached to the slave, and without him, nothing is owed.
5
Slave dies after choosing ransom
If the master had already chosen ransom before the slave's death, the obligation transfers from the slave to the master's personal liability. The ransom must still be paid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جس چیز کو آقا نے اختیار کر لیا ولی جنایت کو دوسری چیز اختیار کرنے کا حق نہیں وأيهما اختاره وفعله لاشيء لولى الجناية غيره أما الدفع فلأن حقه متعلق به فإذا خلى بينه وبين الرقبة سقط وأما الفداء فلأنه لا حق له إلا الأرش فإذا أوفاه حقه سلم العبد له فإن لم يختر شيئا حتى مات العبد بطل حق المجنى عليه لفوات محل حقه على ما بيناه وإن مات بعد ما اختار الفداء لم يبر التحول الحق من رقبة العبد إلى ذمة المولى

ترجمہ اور آقا نے ان دونوں میں سے جس کو اختیار کر لیا اور اس کو انجام دیدیا تو ولی جنایت کے لئے کچھ اس کا غیر نہیں ہے بہر حال غلام دینا پس اس لئے کہ ولی کا حق غلام کے ساتھ متعلق ہے پس جب ولی جنایت اور غلام کے درمیان تخلیہ کر دیا تو مطالبہ کا حق ساقط ہو گیا اور بہر حال فدیہ دینا پس اس لئے کہ ولی کا کوئی حق ارش کے علاوہ نہیں ہے پس جب آقا نے ولی کا حق پورا کر دیا تو غلام آقا کے لئے صحیح سالم رہے گا پس اگر آقا نے کچھ اختیار نہیں کیا یہاں تک کہ غلام مر گیا تو مجنی علیہ کا حق باطل ہو گیا، اس کے حق کا محل فوت ہونے کی وجہ نے اس تفصیل کے مطابق جس کو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اگر غلام مرا ہو بعد اس کے کہ آقا فدیہ دینا اختیار کرے تو آقا بری نہ ہو گا حق کے متحول ہونے کی وجہ سے غلام کی گردن سے آقا کے ذمہ کی جانب۔

تشریح آقا کو مذکورہ دونوں چیزوں میں اختیار ہے اس نے جو نے کو اختیار کر لیا تو ولی جنایت کا کوئی اور حق نہیں رہا۔ یعنی غلام دیدیا تو ارش کا حق نہیں رہا اور دیتی تو غلام لینے کا حق نہیں رہا۔ کیونکہ غلام دینے کی صورت میں جنایت کا حق غلام کی ذات کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اور جب آقا نے غلام اس کو دیدیا تو اس کا حق ادا ہو گیا لہذا اب مزید کے مطالبہ کا حق نہیں رہا اور اگر آقا نے فدیہ ادا کیا ہو تو چونکہ ولی جنایت کا حق بقد را رش تھا جو اس کو مل چکا ہے اور جب ولی کا حق اس کو مل گیا تو غلام آقا کے پاس رہے گا۔ اور ابھی ماقبل میں مسئلہ گذرا ہے کہ اگر غلام مر جائے اور ابھی آقا نے دونوں میں سے کسی کا انتخاب نہیں کیا تھا تو چونکہ اصل واجب غلام ہے اور اب غلام مر گیا ہے لہذا و جوب ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ محل وجوب ختم ہو گیا ہے۔ اور اگر آقا، فدیہ دینا منظور کر چکا تھا اور پھر غلام مر جائے تو اب فدیہ واجب رہے گا۔ کیونکہ اب دولتی جنایت کا حق غلام سے منتقل ہو کر مدیہ کی جانب آچکا ہے جس کی ادائیگی کا ذمہ دار آتا ہے۔
And whichever of the two he chooses and executes, there is nothing else for the guardian of the criminal injury. As for giving the slave, because his right is attached to him; so when he leaves between him and the slave (surrender), his right drops. As for the ransom, because he has no right except the compensation; so when he fulfills his right, the slave remains for the master. If he does not choose anything until the slave dies, the right of the victim becomes void because the place of his right is lost, according to what we have explained. If he dies after he has chosen the ransom, the master is not freed because the right has transferred from the neck of the slave to the liability of the master. Translation: And if the master chooses one of the two and executes it, the guardian has no claim to the other. So if he gives the slave, the right is satisfied; if he pays the ransom, the right is also satisfied. If the master makes no choice and the slave dies, the guardian's right is void. If the master had already chosen ransom and then the slave dies, the ransom remains obligatory.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof explaining the master's options when his slave commits a crime. The master can either surrender the slave to the victim's guardian or pay the ransom (fidya). Once he does one, the guardian has no further claim. If the slave dies before any choice, the right of the guardian is lost because it was attached to the slave. If the master had chosen ransom before the slave died, the obligation transfers to the master's liability.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidya): The ransom paid by the master to free the slave from liability for the crime.
ولی‌الجِنایۃ (wali al-jinaya): The guardian of the victim (or the victim himself) who has the right to claim retribution or compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The master is freed from all obligation.
B) The ransom must still be paid because the right has transferred to the master's liability.
C) The guardian can demand the slave's corpse.
D) The master must surrender a different slave.

Key Takeaway
The master must choose one option; failure to do so before the slave's death voids the guardian's right, but choosing ransom transfers the obligation to the master.

Recurrence of Crime After Ransom: Same Rules Apply
Explains the ruling on a slave's recurrence of crime after ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's recurrence of crime after ransom and explain why the second crime is treated as a new offence.

Core Idea
After ransom, the slave is purified; a second crime is a fresh start, not a continuation.

In this passage, al-Quduri clarifies what happens when a slave commits another crime after the master has already paid ransom for a previous one. The key principle is that payment of ransom erases the first crime, making the slave legally innocent again. Therefore, any subsequent crime is treated as an entirely new incident, and the master again faces the same choice: surrender the slave or pay ransom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Determine what act triggers the ruling: a slave commits a new crime after the master has paid ransom for a prior crime.
The crime may be of the same or different type; the ruling is the same.
2
State the ruling
The ruling for the second crime is identical to the first: the master may choose to pay ransom again or surrender the slave.
This is a direct statement from al-Quduri: 'حكم الجناية الثانية كحكم الجناية الأولى'.
3
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The payment of ransom purifies the slave, undoing the first crime. Legally, it is as if the first crime never occurred.
The text says: 'جعل كأن لم يكن' (makes it as if it never happened).
4
Apply the rule
Treat the second crime as an entirely new beginning, giving the master the same options as before.
This prevents the master from claiming the second crime is a continuation to avoid liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعادہ جنایت کی صورت میں پہلے والا حکم جاری ہوگا قال فإن عاد فجنى كان حكم الجناية الثانية كحكم الجناية الأولى معناه بعد القداء لأنه لما ظهر عن الجناية بالفداء جعل كأن لم يكن وهذا ابتداء جناية

ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر مجرم لوٹا پس جنایت کی تو جنایت ثانیہ کا حکم جنایت اولی کے حکم کے مثل ہے اس کے معنی میں فدیہ ادا کرنے کے بعد اس لئے کہ غلام جب جنایت سے پاک ہو گیا فدیہ ادا کرنے کے ذریعہ تو جنایت کو نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں کر دیا گیا اور یہ پہلی جنایت ہوئی ۔

تشریح اگر آقا غلام کا فدیہ ادا کر چکا ہے لیکن غلام نے دوبارہ پھر جنایت کی تو اب بھی وہی حکم ہوگا۔ جو پہلی ، جنایت کی صورت میں بیان کر دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ جب پہلی جنایت کا فدیہ ادا کر چکا تو غلام جرم سے پاک وصاف ہو چکا ہے گویا کہ اس نے جنایت ہی نہیں کی ۔ اور یہ گویا اس کی پہلی جنایت ہے۔
Recurrence of crime: the same rule applies. He (al-Quduri) said: If he returns and commits a crime, the ruling of the second crime is like the ruling of the first. Its meaning: after payment of ransom, because when the slave becomes free from the crime by paying ransom, it is as if it never happened. And this is a new crime. Translation: Al-Quduri said: If the criminal returns and commits a crime, the ruling of the second crime is like the first. After paying ransom, the slave is purified, so the second crime is treated as a new first crime.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof clarifying what happens if a slave commits another crime after the master has paid ransom for a previous crime. The payment of ransom erases the first crime, making the slave legally as if he never committed it. Therefore, the second crime is treated as an entirely new occurrence, and the master again has the choice to surrender the slave or pay ransom.

Key Terms
اعادہ (i'aada): Recurrence or repetition of a crime after it has been resolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The guardian of the first crime must be consulted.

Key Takeaway
Payment of ransom for a slave's crime erases it; a subsequent crime is treated as an entirely new incident.

Two Crimes by a Slave: Master's Options and Qiyas Proof
Ruling with proof using qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a slave commits two crimes and explain the qiyas to successive debts that justifies it.

Core Idea
A slave's neck can bear multiple crimes like a debtor bears multiple debts; master may surrender or pay ransom for all.

When a slave commits two separate crimes, a question arises: does the first crime block the second from attaching to the slave? The Hanafi school answers with a clear analogy to debts. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the qiyas that supports it, giving you the framework to handle multiple claims against a slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The slave commits two crimes. What is the ruling? The master has two options: surrender the slave to both guardians (who divide him proportionally) or pay ransom for both.
Note that the ruling is an option (takhyeer), not a single obligation.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The author cites an analogy (qiyas) to successive debts (al-duyun al-mutalahiqa). The attachment of the first crime does not prevent the second, just as successive debts attach to a debtor.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illa (effective cause) is explicit.
3
Analyze the illa
The effective cause is that the attachment of a right to the slave's neck (or a debtor's liability) does not prevent another right from attaching. This is extracted from the general principle that ownership (of the master) does not block crime attachment, so the first victim's right is even less likely to block.
The argument uses a minore ad maius (a fortiori) reasoning.
4
Apply the ruling to practice
If the master surrenders the slave, the guardians divide the slave's value proportionally according to their respective diya amounts. They may sell the slave and split the proceeds.
The slave is not physically divided; the division is of the value.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dimension
The passage notes that this ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Some schools may hold that only the first crime attaches, but the Hanafi position uses the qiyas to support multiple attachments.
The text does not detail the opposing view, but the Hanafi proof is clearly presented.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو جنا بیتیں کرلیں تو آقا کر وہ غلام ولی جناتین کے حوالے کرنے میں مارش تاوان ) ادا کرنے میں اختیار ہے قال وإن جنى جنايتين قيل للمولى إما أن تدفعه إلى ولى الجنايتين يقتسمانه على قدر حقيهما وإما أن تفديه بارش كل واحد منهم لأن تعلق الأولى برقبته لا يمنع تعلق الثانية بها كالديون المتلاحقة ألا ترى أن ملك المولى لم يمنع تعلق الجناية فحق المجنى عليه الأول أولى أن لا يمنع ومعنى قوله على قدر حقيهما على قدر أرش جنايتيهما

ترجمہ 14 مقدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر غلام نے دو جنایتیں کیں تو آقا سے کہا جائے گا کہ یا تو تو غلام کو دونوں جناتوں کے ولی کو دیدے جس کو وہ دونوں اپنے حق کے بقدر تقسیم کر لیں گے اور یا غلام کا فدیہ دیدے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے ارش کے بقدر اس لئے کہ پہلی جنایت کا غلام کی گردن سے متعلق ہونا اس کی گردن سے دوسری جنایت کے تعلق کو نہیں روکے گا۔ جیسے پے در پے قرضے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ آقا کی ملک جنایت کے تعلق کو نہیں روکتی تو پہلے مجنی علیہ کا حق بدرجہ اولی نہیں روکے گا اور قدوری کے قول على قدر حقيهما، کے معنی علی قدر ارش جنایتیھما کے ہیں۔

تشریح اگر غلام نے دو جنایتیں کی ہوں مثلاً خالد کو خطا قتل کر دیا اور ساجد کو بھی ۔ خطا قتل کر دیا تو اب بھی آقا کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو دونوں مقتول کے اولیاء کو اپنا مجرم غلام سپر د کر دے اور وہ حصہ اسد اس غلام کو قسیم کر لیں اور آقا چاہے تو ان دونوں کی دیت دیدے اور غلام کو رکھ لے کیونکہ خالد کو قتل کرنے سے ساجد کو قتل کرنے کا جرم قابل عضو نہ ہو گا۔ جیسے آقا کا ملک ہونے کے باوجود قتل خالد کی جنایت کا تعلق ممتنع نہیں ہوا۔ اسی طرح پہلی جنایت متعلق ہونے سے دوسری جنایت کا اس کی گردن سے متعلق ہونا ممنوع نہ ہوگا جیسے اگر غلام نے قرض لیا تو وہ اس کی گردن سے متعلق ہوگا۔ اور اگر دوبارہ سہ بارہ پھر لیا تو وہ بھی اسی کی گردن سے متعلق ہو گا۔
If he commits two crimes, the master has the choice: either hand over the slave to the guardians of the two crimes to divide him according to their rights, or ransom him by paying the compensation for each one. This is because the attachment of the first crime to his neck does not prevent the attachment of the second, like successive debts. Do you not see that the master's ownership did not prevent the attachment of the crime? So the right of the first victim is even less likely to prevent. Meaning of 'according to their rights' means according to the compensation of their crimes. Translation: If a slave commits two crimes, the master is told: either give the slave to the guardians of the two crimes who will divide him according to their respective rights, or pay the ransom for each. The first crime's attachment does not block the second, analogous to successive debts. Just as the master's ownership does not block the crime's attachment, the first victim's right certainly does not block the second.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof using analogy (qiyas) to explain the master's options when a slave commits two crimes. The master can either surrender the slave to both guardians, who will divide the slave proportionally according to the compensation amounts, or pay the full ransom for both and keep the slave. The proof is that multiple claims can attach to the slave just as successive debts can attach to a debtor. The master's ownership does not prevent a crime's attachment, so the first victim's right cannot prevent the second.

Key Terms
دیت (diya): Blood money or compensation paid for homicide or injury.
قسیم (qasim): To divide the slave proportionally among the guardians based on their compensation rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, when a slave commits two crimes, the master can:
A) Surrender the slave for the first crime and pay ransom for the second.
B) Surrender the slave to both guardians to be divided proportionally, or pay ransom for both.
C) Only pay ransom for both; surrender is not allowed.
D) The slave must be executed.

Key Takeaway
A slave's neck can bear multiple crime attachments, just as a debtor bears multiple debts; the master may choose to surrender the slave for division or pay ransom for all.

Repetition of Jinaya by a Slave After Fidyah
Ruling on slave's repeated offense after ransom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a slave's repeated jinaya after fidyah and identify the master's options.

Core Idea
After fidyah, each jinaya is independent; the master's options reset entirely.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi slave liability. When a master pays fidyah (ransom) for his slave's crime, the slave's liability is extinguished as if the crime never occurred. If the slave then commits another jinaya, it is treated as a wholly new offense. The master again has the same choices: hand over the slave or pay a fresh fidyah. This ruling prevents accumulation of liability and ensures clarity in sequential offenses.

Guided Path
1
Confirm the prerequisite: first jinaya settled
The ruling applies only if the master paid fidyah (not handed over the slave) for the first offense, retaining ownership. If the slave was handed over, the master loses ownership and the scenario changes.
2
Recognize the independence of the second offense
After fidyah, the slave is cleared of all liability from the first jinaya. Thus the second crime is treated as a new, independent offense.
This prevents double counting.
3
Identify the master's renewed options
The master again has the choice to either (a) hand over the slave to the victim's heirs, or (b) pay a fresh fidyah equivalent to the arsh or diyah for the new offense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعادہ جنایت کی صورت میں پہلے والا حکم جاری ہوگا
قال فإن عاد فجنى كان حكم الجناية الثانية كحكم الجناية الأولى معناه بعد القداء لأنه لما ظهر عن الجناية بالفداء جعل كأن لم يكن وهذا ابتداء جناية ترجمہ قدوری نے فرمایا پس اگر مجرم لوٹا پس جنایت کی تو جنایت ثانیہ کا حکم جنایت اولی کے حکم کے مثل ہے اس کے معنی میں فدیہ ادا کرنے کے بعد اس لئے کہ غلام جب جنایت سے پاک ہو گیا فدیہ ادا کرنے کے ذریعہ تو جنایت کو نہ ہونے کے درجہ میں کر دیا گیا اور یہ پہلی جنایت ہوئی ۔ تشریح اگر آقا غلام کا فدیہ ادا کر چکا ہے لیکن غلام نے دوبارہ پھر جنایت کی تو اب بھی وہی حکم ہوگا۔ جو پہلی ، جنایت کی صورت میں بیان کر دیا گیا ہے کیونکہ جب پہلی جنایت کا فدیہ ادا کر چکا تو غلام جرم سے پاک وصاف ہو چکا ہے گویا کہ اس نے جنایت ہی نہیں کی ۔ اور یہ گویا اس کی پہلی جنایت ہے۔
Ruling on the repetition of the crime: the same previous ruling applies. He (al-Quduri) said: If he returns and commits a crime, the ruling of the second crime is like the ruling of the first crime. Its meaning is after payment of fidyah, because when the slave is cleared from the crime by fidyah, it is as if it never happened, and this is a new crime. Translation: al-Quduri said: So if the criminal returns and commits a crime, the ruling of the second crime is similar to the ruling of the first crime. Its meaning after paying the ransom: because the slave when purified from the crime by paying the ransom, then the crime is rendered non-existent, and this is a first crime. Explanation: If the master has paid the ransom for the slave but the slave commits a crime again, the same ruling applies as was stated in the case of the first crime, because when the ransom for the first crime is paid, the slave is pure and clean from the crime, as if he had not committed any crime. And this is as if it is his first crime.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement concerning a slave who, after his master has paid fidyah (ransom) for a previous jinaya (homicide or injury), repeats the offense. The text clarifies that the second jinaya is treated as an entirely new offense, not as a continuation of the first. The master again has the same options: either hand over the slave to the victim's heirs or pay a fresh fidyah. This is because the payment of fidyah for the first jinaya cleanses the slave of that liability, making it as if that crime never occurred. The ruling is from the matn of al-Quduri and is explained in the sharh. The commentary emphasizes that the slave's renewed offense stands independently.

Key Terms
جناية (jinaya): A crime or offense causing bodily harm or death, for which compensation (arsh or diyah) is due.
فداء (fidyah): Ransom payment made by the master to redeem a slave who has committed a jinaya, thereby retaining ownership of the slave.
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for a bodily injury less than homicide, determined by the severity and type of injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave commits a second homicide after his master has paid fidyah for the first, what is the ruling?
A) The second homicide is added to the first liability
B) The second homicide is treated as a new, independent offense
C) The master must pay double the fidyah without choice
D) The slave is automatically freed

Key Takeaway
After fidyah, each jinaya by a slave is treated independently, resetting the master's options completely.

Master's Options for Two Jinayat by a Slave
Ruling on master's choice with two jinayat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the master's options when a slave commits multiple jinayat and explain the legal reasoning using the analogy of successive debts.

Core Idea
Each jinaya attaches independently; second does not cancel first.

When a slave commits two separate crimes, does the first crime absorb the second, or do both liabilities attach independently? The Hanafi school rules that each jinaya attaches to the slave's neck like successive debts, giving the master a choice to either hand over the slave (divided among heirs) or ransom the slave by paying compensation for each crime.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's two options
Read the text to find the two possibilities: hand over the slave to the heirs of both victims (who divide the slave proportionally) or pay the full arsh for each offense and keep the slave.
2
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The text compares multiple jinayat to successive debts (duyun mutalāḥiqah). Both attach to the slave's neck independently; the first does not prevent the second.
3
Understand the proportionality
When the master chooses to hand over the slave, the heirs divide the slave's value in proportion to their respective arsh (compensation).
4
Recognize the scope
This ruling applies to any number of jinayat, not just two, and covers both homicide (diyah) and injuries (arsh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دو جنا بیتیں کرلیں تو آقا کر وہ غلام ولی جناتین کے حوالے کرنے میں مارش تاوان ) ادا کرنے میں اختیار ہے 
قال وإن جني جنايتين قيل للمولى إما أن تدفعه إلى ولى الجنايتين يقتسمانه على قدر حقيهما وإما أن تفديه بارش كل واحد منهم لأن تعلق الأولى برقبته لا يمنع تعلق الثانية بها كالديون المتلاحقة ألا ترى أن ملك المولى لم يمنع تعلق الجناية فحق المجنى عليه الأول أولى أن لا يمنع ومعنى قوله على قدر حقيهما على قدر أرش جنايتيهما ترجمہ 14 مقدوری نے فرمایا اور اگر غلام نے دو جنایتیں کیں تو آقا سے کہا جائے گا کہ یا تو تو غلام کو دونوں جناتوں کے ولی کو دیدے جس کو وہ دونوں اپنے حق کے بقدر تقسیم کر لیں گے اور یا غلام کا فدیہ دیدے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے ارش کے بقدر اس لئے کہ پہلی جنایت کا غلام کی گردن سے متعلق ہونا اس کی گردن سے دوسری جنایت کے تعلق کو نہیں روکے گا۔ جیسے پے در پے قرضے کیا آپ نہیں دیکھتے کہ آقا کی ملک جنایت کے تعلق کو نہیں روکتی تو پہلے مجنی علیہ کا حق بدرجہ اولی نہیں روکے گا اور قدوری کے قول على قدر حقيهما، کے معنی علی قدر ارش جنایتیھما کے ہیں۔ تشریح اگر غلام نے دو جنایتیں کی ہوں مثلاً خالد کو خطا قتل کر دیا اور ساجد کو بھی ۔ خطا قتل کر دیا تو اب بھی آقا کو اختیار ہے اگر چاہے تو دونوں مقتول کے اولیاء کو اپنا مجرم غلام سپر د کر دے اور وہ حصہ اسد اس غلام کو قسیم کر لیں اور آقا چاہے تو ان دونوں کی دیت دیدے اور غلام کو رکھ لے کیونکہ خالد کو قتل کرنے سے ساجد کو قتل کرنے کا جرم قابل عضو نہ ہو گا۔ جیسے آقا کا ملک ہونے کے باوجود قتل خالد کی جنایت کا تعلق ممتنع نہیں ہوا۔ اسی طرح پہلی جنایت متعلق ہونے سے دوسری جنایت کا اس کی گردن سے متعلق ہونا ممنوع نہ ہوگا جیسے اگر غلام نے قرض لیا تو وہ اس کی گردن سے متعلق ہوگا۔ اور اگر دوبارہ سہ بارہ پھر لیا تو وہ بھی اسی کی گردن سے متعلق ہو گا۔
If he commits two crimes, the master is told: either hand him over to the heirs of the two crimes, and they will divide him according to their rights, or ransom him with the compensation (arsh) for each one of them, because the attachment of the first to his neck does not prevent the attachment of the second to it, like successive debts. Do you not see that the master's ownership does not prevent the attachment of the crime, so the right of the first victim is even more deserving not to prevent. And the meaning of his statement 'according to their rights' is according to the measure of the arsh of their two crimes. Translation: Al-Quduri said: And if the slave committed two crimes, then the master will be told: either hand the slave over to the heirs of both crimes, and they will divide him according to the measure of their rights, or ransom the slave with the measure of the arsh of each of them. Explanation: If a slave commits two crimes, e.g., he accidentally killed Khalid and also accidentally killed Sajid, then the master still has the option: if he wishes, he may hand over the guilty slave to both heirs of the slain, and they will divide the slave among themselves in shares, and if he wishes, he may pay both their diyahs and keep the slave, because the crime of killing Sajid does not become absorbed by killing Khalid. Just as the master's ownership did not prevent the attachment of the crime of killing Khalid, similarly the attachment of the first crime does not prevent the attachment of the second crime to his neck, like if the slave took a loan, it attaches to his neck, and if he took it again and again, it also attaches to his neck.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the master's options when a slave commits two separate jinayat (e.g., killing two people). The master retains the same choice as in a single jinaya: he may either hand over the slave to the victims' heirs, who will divide the slave's value in proportion to their respective arsh (compensation amounts), or he may pay the full arsh for both offenses and keep the slave. The key legal reasoning is that the first jinaya's attachment to the slave's neck does not prevent the second jinaya from attaching as well, analogous to successive debts. Just as a slave's capacity to incur debts is not exhausted by the first loan, so too multiple jinayat can accumulate. The example given is a slave who has accidentally killed two different people; the crime of one does not absorb the other. The master may pay full diyah for both or hand over the slave to be divided among the heirs.

Key Terms
جنایتان (jinayatayn): Two separate crimes (homicides or injuries) committed by a slave.
دیون متلاحقة (duyun mutalāḥiqah): Successive debts: debts incurred one after another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of a slave who commits two homicides, the master may:
A) Only hand over the slave to the first victim's heirs
B) Pay fidyah for one and hand over for the other
C) Either hand over the slave to both heirs or pay fidyah for both
D) The slave is automatically executed

Key Takeaway
Each jinaya attaches independently; the master must account for all, and the first does not absorb the second.

Multiple Victims and Different Injuries
Ruling on proportional division of slave's value among multiple crime victims.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional division of a slave's value among multiple victims of different injuries according to Hanafi diyat rules.

Core Idea
Victims share the slave's value in proportion to their arsh (fixed compensation).

In cases where a single slave commits crimes against multiple persons, the question arises how the victims should be compensated. The Hanafi school rules that the victims divide the slave's value (or the ransom paid by the master) proportionally to the arsh of each injury. This lesson explains the calculation using examples of homicide and eye-gouging, and extends to all injuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The master has two options: hand over the slave to the victims, or pay the full arsh (ransom) for all crimes. We focus on the first scenario.
2
Understand proportional division
When the master hands over the slave, the victims share the slave's value in proportion to their respective arsh amounts. The arsh for each injury is a fixed sum prescribed in the diyat system.
Arsh for life (full diyah) is 100% of the full diyah; arsh for an eye is 50%.
3
Work through the homicide + eye example
If the slave kills one person (arsh = full diyah) and gouges out the eye of another (arsh = half diyah), the total arsh is 1.5 times the full diyah. The slave's price (assumed equal to total arsh) is divided into three equal shares: two for the homicide victim's heir, one for the eye injury victim.
Ratio 2:1 because 1 : 0.5 = 2 : 1
4
Generalize to multiple and different injuries
The same proportional method applies when there are any number of victims and any type of injury (shijaj, wounds, etc.). The slave's price is divided according to the ratio of the arsh of each victim.
The principle is derived from the rule that compensation must be proportionate to harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اپنے حق کے بقدر لینے کا یہ مطلب ہے کہ ان دونوں کے ارش میں جو تناسب ہے اس تناسب سے غلام کی قیمت میں سے لیں گے۔ مثلاً ایک کو ایسا زخم لگایا جس سے پندرہ سو (۵۰۰ لک وپے واجب ہوتے ہیں اور دوسرے کے زخم سے مثلاً تین ہزار ۳۰۰۰ روپے واجب ہوتے تو غلام کی قیمت بھی ان دونوں کے درمیان اخلا عا تقسیم کی جائے گی ۔
اگر بہت سے اشخاص پر جنایت کی تو وہ اپنے سب حصوں کے بقدر غلام کی قیمت سے وصول کریں گے
وإن كانوا جماعة يقتسمون العبد المدفوع على قدر حصصهم وإن فداه فداه بجيع أروشهم لما ذكرنا ولو قتل واحدا وفقأ عين آخر يقتسمانه أثلاثا لأن أرش العين على النصف من أرش النفس وهذا حكم الشجات ترجمہ اور اگر اولیاء ایک جماعت ہو تو وہ لوگ دیئے ہوئے غلام کو اپنے حصوں کے بقدر تقسیم کریں گے اور اگر آقا غلام کا فدیہ دینا منظور کرے تو آقا ان سب کے ارش کے بقدر فدیہ دے گا اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم ذکر کر چکے ہیں ۔ اور اگر ایک کو قتل کیا اور دوسرے کی آنکھ پھوڑ دی تو وہ دونوں غلام کو اعملا یا تقسیم کریں گے اس لئے کہ آنکھ کا ارش نفس کے ارش کا نصف ہے اور اسی طریقہ پر شجات کا حکم ہے ۔ تشریح خلاصہ کلام اگر بہت سے شخصوں کو اس نے زخمی کیا تو وہ سب اپنے حصوں کے بقدر غلام کی قیمت سے وصول کریں گے۔ اور اگر آ قائد یہ ادا کرے تو ارش کا جوفد یہ بیٹھتا ہے وہ ادا کرنا ضروری ہوگا۔ اور نفس کی دیت پوری دیت ہوتی ہے اور آنکھ کی آدھی ، لہذا اگر غلام نے ایک شخص کو تو قتل کر دیا اور ایک کی آنکھ پھوڑ دی تو قیمت کے تین حصے ہوں گے ان میں سے دو ولی نفس کو اور ایک ولی عین کا ہوگا۔ اسی طرح اگر شجات مختلف ہوں تو انہیں کے تناسب سے غلام کی قیمت ان کے درمیان تقسیم کی جائے گی۔ (ومر تفصیلہ فیما سبق ) ۔
The meaning of taking according to their rights is that they will take from the price of the slave in proportion to the ratio between their arsh. For example, if one was wounded such that one thousand five hundred (?) is owed, and the other's wound obligates, for example, three thousand rupees, then the price of the slave will also be divided between them accordingly. If he committed crimes against many persons, they will receive from the price of the slave according to the measure of their shares. And if they are a group, they divide the handed-over slave according to their shares. And if he ransoms him, he ransoms him with all their arsh, for the reason we mentioned. And if he killed one and gouged out the eye of another, they divide the slave into thirds, because the arsh of the eye is half of the arsh of the life. And this is the ruling for injuries. Translation: And if the heirs are a group, they will divide the given slave according to their shares. And if the master wishes to ransom the slave, he will ransom him with the arsh of all of them, for the same reason. And if he killed one and gouged out the eye of another, they will divide the slave into three parts, because the arsh of the eye is half the arsh of the life, and the same rule applies to injuries. Explanation: Summary: If he wounded many persons, they all receive from the price of the slave according to their shares. And if he pays fidyah, he must pay the full amount of arsh. And the diyah for life is full diyah, and for the eye it is half. So if a slave killed one person and gouged out the eye of another, the price will be three parts: two for the heir of the life and one for the heir of the eye. Similarly, if there are various injuries, they are divided according to the same proportion.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that first provides a numerical example from the previous lesson (two jinayat with different arsh amounts) and then expands to cases involving many victims and mixed injuries. The key rule is that when a slave commits crimes against multiple persons, the victims (or their heirs) share the slave's value in proportion to their respective arsh. If the master chooses to hand over the slave, the victims divide the slave proportionally. If the master pays fidyah, he must pay the total arsh for all victims. A specific example: if the slave killed one person (full diyah) and gouged out the eye of another (half diyah), the slave's price is divided into three shares: two thirds for the homicide victim's heir, one third for the eye injury victim. This proportionate division applies to all injuries (shijaj) as well.

Key Terms
شجات (shijāj): Head wounds or injuries; technically, wounds that expose the skull. Here used generally for bodily injuries.
أثلاثا (athlathan): In thirds; dividing the slave's value into three equal parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Equally between the two victims
B) Two-thirds to the homicide victim's heir, one-third to the eye injury victim
C) All to the homicide victim
D) The slave is freed

Key Takeaway
Victims share the slave's value in proportion to their fixed arsh compensation.

Master's Option to Differentiate When Jinayat Have Different Causes
Ruling on master's option when slave commits multiple jinayat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule concerning a master's option when a slave commits multiple different jinayat, and distinguish it from the case of a single victim with multiple heirs.

Core Idea
Different causes create separate rights, allowing differentiated treatment; unified cause forbids differentiation.

This passage explains a master's right to choose between paying fidyah or handing over the slave to different victims when the slave has committed separate crimes. The key principle is that each crime is an independent cause, giving rise to a distinct right. The passage contrasts this with a situation where one victim has multiple heirs: here the right is single, so the master must treat all heirs identically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Separate the case of multiple victims (different crimes) from the case of one victim with multiple heirs.
The contrast is between multiplicity of causes vs. unity of cause.
2
Recognize the 'illa: multiplicity vs. unity of causes
The text explicitly states that rights differ due to differing causes (al-huquq mukhtalifa bi-ikhtilaf asbabiha). In the heirs case, the cause is one, so the right is one.
The 'illa (legal cause) is the multiplicity or unity of the jinaya.
3
Apply the rule to each scenario
For different causes: master may pay fidyah for some and hand over for others. For a single cause: master must treat all heirs uniformly; he cannot pay fidyah to one and hand over to another.
The ruling is a direct consequence of the nature of the right.
4
Understand the underlying principle
Rights are attached to their causes; the cause determines the nature and number of rights. This is a fundamental Hanafi usul principle.
Compare with other areas where multiplicity of causes creates multiple obligations.
5
Note the practical outcome
The master's option is not arbitrary; it is based on the distinctness of the legal causes. Different crimes give him independent options per crime.
This ruling prevents injustice by allowing proportional satisfaction of each victim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جب جنایات مختلف قسم کی ہوں تو آقا کو کیا اختیار ہے
وللمولى أن يفدى من بعضهم ويدفع إلى بعضهم مقدار ما تعلق به حقه من العبد لأن الحقوق مختلفة باختلاف أسبابها وهى الجنايات المختلفة بخلاف مقتول كعبد إذا كان له وليان ولم يكن له أن بفدى من أحدهما ويدفع إلى الآخر لأن الحق متحد لاتحاد سببه وهى الجناية المتحدة والحق يجب للمقتول ثم للوارث خلافة عنه فلايملك التفريق في موجبها
ترجمہ اور مولیٰ کو حق ہے کہ ان میں سے بعض کو فدیہ دیدے اور ان میں سے بعض کو غلام دیدے اس قدر کہ اس کا حق غلام کے ساتھ متعلق ہے اس لئے کہ حقوق مختلف ہیں ان کے اسباب کے مختلف ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ اسباب مختلف جنایات ہیں۔ بخلاف غلام کے مقتول کے جب کہ اس کے دو ولی ہوں تو آقا کو حق نہ ہو گا کہ ان میں سے ایک کو فدیہ دے اور دوسرے کو غلام حوالہ کرے اس لئے کہ حق ایک ہے اس کے سبب کے ایک ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ سبب ایک جنایت ہے اور حق مقتول کے لئے واجب ہوتا ہے پھر وارث کو اس کی وراثت کی بنا پر ملتا ہے تو آقا کو اختیار نہیں کہ اس کی موجبات میں تفریق کرے
When the crimes are of different types, what option does the master have? And the master has the right to pay fidyah for some of them and hand over to some of them the amount of his right that is attached to the slave, because the rights are different due to the difference of their causes, and these are the different crimes. Unlike a killed slave (i.e., a slave who is a victim) when he has two heirs, the master does not have the right to pay fidyah for one and hand over the slave to the other, because the right is one due to the unity of its cause, and that cause is one crime, and the right is due to the slain person, then to the heir by way of succession from him, so he does not have the authority to differentiate in its consequences. Translation: And the master has the right to pay fidyah for some of them and hand over the slave to some of them to the extent that his right is attached to the slave, because the rights are different due to the difference of their causes, and these causes are the different crimes. Unlike a killed slave when he has two heirs, the master does not have the right to pay fidyah for one and hand over the slave to the other, because the right is one due to the unity of its cause, and that cause is one crime, and the right is due to the killed person, then to the heir by inheritance from him, so he does not have the authority to differentiate in its requirements.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that gives the master additional flexibility when the slave commits different types of jinayat against multiple victims. The master may choose to pay fidyah for some victims and hand over the slave to others, because each jinaya is a distinct cause giving rise to a separate right. However, this is contrasted with a case where a single victim (a slave) has multiple heirs: in that case, the master cannot pay fidyah to one heir and hand over to another, because the right is one (unified) arising from a single jinaya. The right belongs to the victim, and the heirs inherit it collectively; therefore the master must treat all heirs the same. This ruling emphasizes that the cause (sabab) determines the nature of the right: multiple jinayat create multiple rights, allowing differentiation; a single jinaya creates a single right, forbidding differentiation among heirs.

Key Terms
سبب (sabab): Legal cause or reason that gives rise to a right. Here, each jinaya is a separate sabab.
موجب (mūjib): Consequence or requirement of the right. Here, the master's choice to hand over or pay fidyah is part of the requirements of the right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which case can a master pay fidyah to one claimant and hand over the slave to another?
A) When there is a single victim with multiple heirs
B) When the slave commits a single crime against one victim
C) When the slave commits different jinayat against different victims
D) The master never has this option

Key Takeaway
The multiplicity of legal causes (asbab) allows separate treatment of each right; unity of cause forbids differentiation.

Master's Right to Differentiate Between Victims When Slave Commits Multiple Crimes
Explains when a master can differentiate between victims for a slave's crimes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for when a master can differentiate between victims of a slave's crimes and identify when differentiation is prohibited.

Core Idea
Differentiation allowed only when crimes differ; unity of cause forbids differential treatment.

This lesson examines the master's options when his slave commits crimes against multiple individuals. The key is whether the obligations arise from a single cause or multiple causes. Understanding this distinction ensures correct application of diyat and compensation rules.

Guided Path
1
Identify the master's basic liability
When a slave commits a crime, the master may either hand over the slave or pay compensation. This is the baseline right.
This assumes the master does not choose to relinquish the slave entirely.
2
Distinguish between multiple crimes and single crime
If the slave commits multiple crimes of different types (e.g., murder and blinding), each crime creates a separate cause of obligation. The master may differentiate in how he satisfies each obligation.
Differentiation means paying for one crime and surrendering the slave for another.
3
Apply the unity of cause principle
If the slave kills a single person, even if that person has multiple heirs, the cause (the killing) is one. Therefore, the master cannot treat the heirs differently; he must satisfy them all in the same way.
The right originally belongs to the victim and passes by succession to the heirs, so the cause remains one.
4
Derive the ruling
When crimes are different, differentiation is permissible. When the crime is one (same victim), differentiation is not permissible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الديات
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد - ۱۵ حق متحد ہے حق کے سبب کے متحد ہونے کی وجہ سے اور وہ ایک جنایت ہے اور حق مقتول کے لئے واجب ہوتا ہے پھر مقتول سے خلافت کے طریقہ پر وارث کے لئے ثابت ہوتا ہے تو آقا موجب جنایت میں تفریق کا مالک نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح اگر جنایات مختلف ہیں مثلاً ایک کو غلام نے قتل کیا ہے اور دوسرے کی آنکھ پھوڑی ہے تو آقا جیسے یہاں یہ کر سکتا ہے کہ دونوں کو مجرم غلام دیدے یا فدیہ میں دونوں کا ارش ادا کر دے، اسی طرح آقا کو یہ بھی حق ہے کہ ایک کو غلام کا فدیہ دیدے اور دوسرے کے حق کے بقدر دوسرے کو غلام دیدے اس لئے کہ یہاں اسباب یعنی جنایات مختلف ہیں۔ لیکن اگر غلام نے ایک شخص کو قتل کیا ہو اور مقتول کے دو ولی ہوں تو چونکہ یہاں مقتول ایک ہے تو دونوں ولیوں کے حق کے اسباب مختلف نہیں بلکہ سبب واحد ہے اس لئے آقا یہ نہیں کر سکتا کہ ایک کو فدیہ دیدے اور دوسرے کو غلام دیدے بلکہ یا تو ان دونوں کو فدیہ دے گا یا غلام ان دونوں کو دے گا یعنی آقا کو اتحاد سبب کی وجہ سے تفریق کا حق نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ابتداء اصل حق تو مقتول کا ہوتا ہے پھر خلافت کے طور پر ورثاء کو ملتا ہے تو گویا صاحب حق بھی ایک ہے اور سبب بھی ایک ہے اس لئے تفریق درست نہ ہوگی۔
The Book of Diyat. Ashraf al-Bidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume 15. The right is unified due to the unity of its cause, and that cause is one crime. And the right is established for the victim, then for the heir via succession. So the master does not possess the right to differentiate in the cause of the crime. Explanation: If the crimes are different, e.g., a slave killed one person and blinded another, then the master can do such that he gives the slave to both, or pays the compensation (arsh) for both. Similarly, the master also has the right to give compensation for one and hand over the slave for the other, because here the causes (i.e., the crimes) are different. But if the slave killed one person and the victim has two guardians (wali), then since the victim is one, the rights of the two guardians do not have different causes; rather, the cause is one. Therefore, the master cannot give compensation to one and the slave to the other; rather, he must either give compensation to both or give the slave to both. That is, due to the unity of cause, the master does not have the right to differentiate. Because initially the original right belongs to the victim, then it transfers to the heirs via succession. So essentially, the right-holder is one and the cause is one, hence differentiation is not valid.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage from the Urdu commentary on Al-Hidayah discusses the master's rights when his slave commits crimes against multiple individuals. The key principle is that the master's ability to differentiate between victims depends on whether the crimes are of different types or against different persons. If the crimes are different (e.g., murder and blinding), the master can choose to pay compensation for one and hand over the slave for the other, because the causes of obligation are different. However, if the slave kills a single person who has multiple heirs (guardians), all heirs have the same right because the cause is the same: the same victim. Therefore, the master cannot treat them differently; he must either pay compensation to all or hand over the slave to all jointly. The rationale is that the right originally belongs to the victim and then passes to the heirs by succession, so the right-holder is effectively one and the cause is one. This ruling is consistent with the Hanafi principle that rights attached to a unified cause cannot be apportioned differently.

Key Terms
قتل (qatl): unlawful killing
ولي (wali): guardian of the victim who has the right to demand qisas or diyat
أرش (arsh): compensation for bodily injury not amounting to death

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the situation where a slave kills one person who has two heirs (guardians), what rights does the master have?
A) He can pay compensation to one and give the slave to the other.
B) He must either pay compensation to both or give the slave to both.
C) He must give the slave to both and pay no compensation.
D) He can choose to do nothing.

Key Takeaway
When a slave commits multiple crimes, differentiation is allowed only if the crimes are different; unity of cause demands uniform treatment.
