Diyat — Blood Money
intermediate
8 min
Four Actions That Affect Master's Option: Beating, Intercourse with Virgin, Marriage, Intercourse with Non-Virgin
Lists four actions by master that affect his option status after slave's crime.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four actions that make the master mukhtar and explain the reasoning (ta'lil) behind each, distinguishing between actions that cause a real decrease in value and those that do not.

Core Idea
The master's option to pay ransom is triggered only by actions that actually reduce the slave's value, not by mere legal defects.

In this passage, the author lists four actions a master might take after his slave commits a crime. The key question is whether these actions affect the master's option to either pay the victim's ransom or surrender the slave. The rulings hinge on whether the action genuinely reduces the slave's value, which would prejudice the victim's chance to collect from the slave's earnings. Let's examine each case and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
The underlying principle is that the master becomes mukhtar (having the option to pay the ransom) if he detains a part of the slave's value (حبس جزء منه). This is based on the idea that the master's actions that reduce the slave's value prevent the victim from being fully compensated, so the master is then obligated to pay the ransom instead of surrendering the slave.
This principle is applied consistently across all four actions.
2
Analyze the first action (beating)
If the master beats the criminal slave and causes damage (e.g., injury), this directly reduces the slave's value. Therefore, the master becomes mukhtar. Note that he must have known of the crime at the time of beating.
The passage says: 'لأنه حبس جزء منه' – because he detained a part of him.
3
Analyze the second action (intercourse with virgin)
If the criminal female slave is a virgin and the master has intercourse with her (even without pregnancy), this removes virginity, which reduces her value. Thus, the master becomes mukhtar. The act itself is decreasing (نفس الوطي منقص).
Pregnancy is not required for this case; the act of intercourse itself is sufficient.
4
Analyze the third action (marriage)
If the master marries the criminal slave to someone, this is only a legal defect (عيب حكمي), not a real physical defect. It does not decrease the slave's actual value, so the master does not become mukhtar.
The passage contrasts this with the previous case: marriage is a defect in a legal sense only.
5
Analyze the fourth action (intercourse with non-virgin)
If the master has intercourse with a non-virgin criminal female slave, according to zahir al-riwayah (the apparent narration), he does not become mukhtar unless pregnancy results. This is because the intercourse itself does not decrease value in a non-virgin (نفس الوطي غير منقص في الثيب). Only if pregnancy occurs (تعلیق) does value decrease, making him mukhtar.
There is an alternative view (ghayr zahir al-riwayah) that may differ, but the relied-upon position is as stated.

لا ينقض من غير إعلاق
ترجمہ اور اگر آقا نے مجرم غلام کو مارا پس اس کو نقصان پہنچا دیا تو آقافدیہ اختیار کرنے والا ہے جب کہ وہ جنایت کو جانتا ہو اس لئے کہ اس نے غلام کا ایک جز روک لیا۔ اور ایسے ہی جب کہ مجرمہ باکرہ ہو پس اس سے وطی کر لی اگر چہ وہ ولی معلق نہ ہو ( حمل کا سبب ) اسی دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں، بخلاف نکاح کرنے کے اس لئے کہ یہ باعتبار حکم غیب ہے، اور بخلاف شیبہ سے وطی کرنے کے ظاہر الروایہ کے مطابق، اس لئے کہ یہ بغیر حمل کے نقصان کا باعث نہیں ہے۔

عیب نہیں ہے۔ -۴- اگر آقا نے نقیہ مجرمہ باندی سے ولی کی ہو تو آقا فدیہ اختیار کرنے والا شمار نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ نقیہ میں نفس ولی منقص نہیں ہے البتہ اگر اس ولی سے حمل ٹھہر جائے تو منتقص ہے۔
Explanation of four issues: And if he struck him and damaged him, then he is mukhtar if he knew of the crime, because he detained a part of him. Similarly, if she was a virgin and he had intercourse with her, even if he did not cause pregnancy, for what we said. Contrary to marriage, because it is a defect in a legal sense. And contrary to intercourse with a non-virgin, according to the apparent narration, because it does not cause decrease without pregnancy. Translation: And if the master struck the criminal slave and caused damage, then the master is one who chooses the ransom, if he knew of the crime, because he detained a part of the slave. And similarly, if the female slave was a virgin and he had intercourse with her, even if he did not cause pregnancy (the cause), for the same reason we mentioned. Contrary to marriage, because it is a defect in a legal sense. And contrary to intercourse with a non-virgin, according to the apparent narration, because it does not cause decrease without pregnancy. Explanation: In this phrase, the author mentioned four issues. (1) If the master beat the criminal slave so that damage occurred, and the master knew of the crime, then in that case the master has detained a part of the slave, so he is considered to have chosen the ransom due to his action. (2) If the female slave is a virgin and she committed a crime, and the master, despite knowing of the crime, had intercourse with her, then he will be considered to have chosen the ransom, even if pregnancy did not occur, because here the actual intercourse is decreasing (the value). (3) If the master married the criminal slave (to someone), then he will not be considered to have chosen the ransom, because marriage, even though legally a defect, is not actually a defect. (4) If the master had intercourse with a non-virgin criminal female slave, then the master will not be considered to have chosen the ransom, because in a non-virgin, the intercourse itself is not decreasing. However, if pregnancy results from this intercourse, then it is decreasing.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage discusses four actions by the master after the slave's crime that affect his option (mukhtar). First, if the master beats the criminal slave and causes damage (e.g., injury), the master becomes mukhtar because he has effectively 'detained a part' of the slave—the slave's value is reduced, which affects the victim's compensation. Second, if the female slave is a virgin and the master has intercourse with her after knowing the crime, he becomes mukhtar even if pregnancy does not occur. The act of intercourse itself diminishes the slave's value by removing virginity. Third, if the master marries the slave (to someone else), he does not become mukhtar. Marriage is considered a defect only legally (hukman), not really (haqiqatan), meaning it does not physically reduce the slave's value. Fourth, if the master has intercourse with a non-virgin female slave, he does not become mukhtar according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) because such intercourse does not cause a decrease in value unless pregnancy occurs. If pregnancy does occur, then it is considered a decrease. These rulings are based on the principle that the master's option is triggered when his actions reduce the slave's value or prevent the victim from receiving full compensation.

Key Terms
بکر (bikr): A virgin female slave.
ثیب (thayyib): A non-virgin female slave.
تعلیق (ta'liq): Pregnancy (lit. suspension, as it is the cause of the slave's value decrease).
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent/well-known narration from the Hanafi imams, as opposed to rare transmissions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the master become mukhtar after intercourse with a non-virgin female slave?
A) Immediately upon intercourse.
B) Only if pregnancy results.
C) Never.
D) If the master knew of the crime.

Key Takeaway
A master becomes mukhtar only when his action actually decreases the slave's value, not when it merely creates a legal defect.
